This list contains a sample (every seventh entry) of the the top 60,000 lemmas from the 
Corpus of Contemporary American English (COCA) (http://corpus.byu.edu/coca/).
You can also donwload an Excel verion: http://www.wordfrequency.info/files/wordlist_60k.xls

Note that this is the *only* frequency list of English that is corrected for a list this large.
All other frequency lists (if they are corrected at all, to remove bad entries) only correct the top 5,000 or 10,000 words.

It is also possible to purchase lists with the 200-300 most frequent collocates for each of the 
60,000 words in the frequency list.


For more information:

http://www.wordfrequency.info: Word frequency lists
http://corpus.byu.edu/coca/: Corpus of Contemporary American English (COCA)
http://davies-linguistics.byu.edu/ : Mark Davies

-------------------------------------------------------------------

Note that there are many lower-frequency words (e.g. #35,000-40,000 and lower) that are probably really NOUN,
but which are tagged as ADJ because they have an ADJ "function" (e.g. a *weight-training* regimen, a *sibilant* consonant). 


freq = frequency in the corpus
dispersion = Juilland's <d> dispersion measure (0-1): how "evenly" the lemma is distributed across the corpus
rank = a function of score (not shown here), but which is calculated as: freq * disp
pos = part of speech (see http://ucrel.lancs.ac.uk/claws7tags.html)
